Inspection Report on the Recovery of Various Areas After Suppressing the Communists (7) 80

Inspection of the Communist Nest in Honghu

(Taxation System) The taxes levied by the communist bandits in Honghu are divided into land tax, business tax, customs duty, and rent. A brief description is given below: (i) Land tax: This tax is collected based on the yield of the fields and the social class of the farmers, calculated annually, and collected in spring and autumn. The tax rate starts at 100 yuan. Rich peasants pay 15 percent of 100 yuan, middle peasants pay 5 percent, poor peasants pay 3 percent, and so on. (ii) Business tax: This tax is levied progressively. Capital between 50 yuan and 200 yuan is taxed at 2 percent, 200 yuan to 300 yuan at 2.5 percent, 300 yuan to 400 yuan at 3 percent, 400 yuan to 500 yuan at 3.5 percent, 500 yuan to 600 yuan at 4 percent, 600 yuan to 800 yuan at 4.5 percent, 800 yuan to 1,000 yuan at 5 percent, and the rest are increased according to the rate. (iii) Customs duty: The Honghu communist bandits set up checkpoints at lake entrances and major roads to collect import and export customs duties. For both exports and imports, they collect 1 percent starting at 50 yuan. Merchants from non-red areas passing through the red areas with capital above 5,000 yuan are required to pay customs duties based on the progressive business tax rate. To alleviate the food shortages in the red areas, the communist bandits exempt import food from customs duties to encourage rice merchants to transport food regularly. (iv) Rent: Houses confiscated by the communist bandits in the bandit areas are distributed to poor and middle peasants living in the countryside along with the land. In major cities and towns, except for those reserved for use by various agencies, the remaining houses are rented out by the "Soviet" at market prices. For privately rented houses, land and property taxes are also levied on the landlords. The above are the communist bandits' regular taxes. Later, due to insufficient income, they concocted various pretexts, creating donations to support the Red Army, exploiting every source of revenue, and imposing exorbitant taxes, making it increasingly difficult for the people in the bandit areas to make a living.

(Red Education) The Honghu communist bandits paid unusual attention to red education, organizing a "Cultural Committee" to specialize in this matter, doing their best to instill communism, and anesthetizing the general ignorant population. Their education methods are divided into two types: social education and national education. Social education is centered on workers' and peasants' clubs, setting up reading rooms, reading classes, lecture halls, and new drama stages to instill communism at all times. In addition, they use various assembly methods to carry out the social education of their red masses. For national education, they set up Lenin Elementary Schools to redify young children and establish night schools or half-day schools to instill communist knowledge in the general uneducated population. Their various plans are extremely meticulous.

(External Transportation) To supplement their material needs, the Honghu communist bandits secretly maintained external transportation. Xindi is their main port of entry and exit, where daily necessities such as rice, grain, and salt are mostly obtained. Personnel dispatched from Shanghai to the bandit areas and the transportation of various machines land at Bailuoji, west of Xindi. The communist bandits pre-dispatch ships to meet them there. Those traveling from Shanghai purchase tickets to Shashi, transfer to bandit ships at Bailuoji midway, and head to the Honghu bandit area. The bandit ships all have secret signals, much like the situation in Liangshan Marsh. As for the bandit area's external trade, merchants handle it from the middle. Merchants traveling back and forth have passes issued by the communist bandits and good citizen certificates issued by government troops as protective charms. When a merchant arrives in the bandit area, they present their pass to pass through. After leaving the bandit area, they hide the pass and present their good citizen certificate to prove their identity in order to avoid danger, forming a subtle commercial relationship. With the above-mentioned unbelievable secret transportation methods, even though government troops were besieging them, the communist bandits' external transportation was still not completely cut off. This is the reason.

(Internal Strife) The Honghu communist bandits have complex internal factions and differing opinions. In addition to the ultra-left communist bandits, there are reorganization factions, the Third Party, the AB Corps, etc. Before the bandit nest was captured, the reorganization faction, the Third Party, and the AB Corps united to overthrow the ultra-left faction, scheduled to launch an uprising on September 15. However, the plan was leaked, and the ultra-left faction preemptively struck. Starting from September 13, they began the so-called anti-rebellion work, arresting more than 1,000 people they considered to be reactionaries. Countless important personnel in the communist bandit party, government, and military were implicated and imprisoned. People were panicking and felt uneasy. When arresting the reactionaries, all the arrested important personnel were smeared with black ash or covered with black cloth, and escorted at night to avoid attention. One or two days before the bandit nest was broken, most of the arrested personnel were executed. In the Xingu area, 700 people were killed in one night. The massacre was so tragic that it made one's hair stand on end. As a result of the communist bandit infighting, the interior was in turmoil, morale was scattered, and the National Army took the opportunity to attack, destroying them with the force of a thunderbolt, and sweeping away the nest in no time.

(Occupy the Mountains or Occupy the Water) During the National Army's suppression, as the Honghu communist bandits' nest was threatened, a fierce dispute arose internally regarding the safety issue. One faction advocated occupying the mountains, believing that occupying the mountains was easy to defend, and strongly advocated abandoning Honghu and fleeing to the mountains of western Hubei or western Hunan. The other faction advocated occupying the water, believing that Honghu was located in central Hubei, with a strategic location, making it easy to develop and retreat, and that it would be enough to confront the National Army. Moreover, it had been operated for several years, and abandoning it would be a pity. The two factions argued inconclusively. In the end, the mountain occupation faction gained the upper hand. He Long selected more than 2,000 elite troops to seek another way out to the west. Wang Yimin and others led the bandit troops to guard Honghu. The "Soviet of the Western Hunan and Hubei Province" moved from Qujiawan to Xingouzu. The main force of the bandit troops was also concentrated here. Later, the 10th Army of Xu Yuanquan launched a large-scale siege of Xingu, wiping them out in one fell swoop. The remnants of the Honghu bandits were quickly cleared within a few days. He Long fled west when his nest was broken.

(Reasons for Failure) The Honghu communist bandits had a great momentum, but they were annihilated in one fell swoop this time. The reasons for their failure are approximately as follows: (i) The officers and soldiers of the Tenth Army, who suppressed the Honghu communist bandits, were exceptionally brave, their plans were meticulous, and their advance was rapid. The communist bandits were a rabble, poorly trained. Once they encountered a strong enemy, they could not take care of both ends. In the Battle of Xingu, the entire army was wiped out. (ii) The communist bandits initially used the abolition of exorbitant taxes, the equal distribution of land, and the relief of the people's suffering to lure the ignorant villagers. As a result, exorbitant taxes were abolished in name but still existed in reality, and the equal distribution of land was nominal rather than real. In addition, the struggle against rich peasants made the farmers uneasy, and arbitrary killings made everyone feel insecure. The suffering of the people in the bandit area was a hundred times worse than before the redification. Although the people dared to be angry under the accumulated power, they did not dare to speak, but the people's hearts were alienated, they realized the fraud, and thought of returning on their own. (iii) Mutual infighting and self-destruction of the barrier. The internal united front was broken, and the National Army's suppression attack became easier. (iv) The defense and attack strategy was inconclusive. The overall plan for defense against the National Army's advance was not completed, and the National Army suddenly advanced, responding in a panic, and the flags were overturned and the tracks were chaotic. Due to these various reasons, the Honghu, which the communist bandits had operated for several years, was recovered, and the elite troops that had gathered for many years were also wiped out at once. (To be continued)

Chen Guohui is Executed 81

The Fujian Pacification Headquarters Announces Chen's Crimes

Fuzhou Correspondence: Chen Guohui, the brigade commander of the mixed brigade of the Fujian Provincial Defense Army, who was previously detained by the Pacification Headquarters, was sentenced to death on the morning of the 23rd at 7:00 AM and taken to the parade ground inside the Donghu Barracks for execution by firing squad. He was killed by a total of five shots. This reporter personally went to observe and saw Chen's body lying supine on the ground, wearing a gray serge suit, blue socks, and slippers. His head was shattered, his chest and abdomen were riddled with holes, his hair was an inch long, and blood flowed all over the ground, a truly tragic sight. It was learned that Chen's execution this time was unknown to all parties beforehand. The public only learned of it after the announcement of his crimes. It is said that the reason for this was that Chen's former subordinates Chen Peiyu and Chen Yucai, etc., recently colluded with local bandits such as Ye Wenliang, Lin Qinglong, Ye Dingguo, and Quan Feifeng in Nan'an, Anxi, Dehua, and Jinjiang counties in southern Fujian, causing large-scale disturbances, attempting to disrupt local security, divide military-civilian relations, and thereby undermine the overall situation. A few days ago, Cai Tingkai returned from the province to Zhangzhou to inspect the situation in various places and telegraphed Jiang Guangnai to execute Chen in order to prevent such people from blackmailing and then dispatch troops to search and suppress the bandits in order to eliminate the bandit disaster. Therefore, after receiving the telegram, Jiang executed Chen by firing squad. The Pacification Headquarters' announcement of Chen's crimes is recorded as follows: "It has been determined that Chen Guohui was originally a reckless and unbridled individual, who took advantage of opportunities to gather in southern Fujian, acting violently and committing all kinds of evil, such as protecting bandits, extorting money, harming the people, imposing exorbitant taxes, creating taxes at will, forcing the cultivation of opium poppies, slaughtering and burning villages, destroying party affairs, and resisting orders with his troops. His various crimes are too numerous to count, and they are all facts that are commonly seen and heard in society, with no possibility of concealment. When our army moved into Fujian, we received complaints from overseas and domestic mass organizations and victims accusing Chen of causing disasters in Fujian, which were piled up a foot high. The head of this army still repeatedly tolerated and exhorted him, hoping that he would repent and reform. Unexpectedly, the criminal persisted in his evil ways, poisoning the local area and resisting orders with his troops as before. Therefore, we took him into custody and presented a report to the Military Affairs Commission of the National Government requesting the organization of a military tribunal. After careful investigation, the evidence was conclusive, and his crimes were unforgivable. The criminal Chen Guohui should be sentenced to death in accordance with Articles 25, 27, 35, 47, and 63 of the Army, Navy, and Air Force Criminal Law and the crimes combined. He will be taken to the execution ground on the 23rd of this month to verify his identity and be executed by firing squad as a warning. This is hereby announced, including the execution by firing squad of the bandit Chen Guohui, a native of Nan'an County, Fujian Province, 35 years old." (December 23)

Huang Yizhu and Others Prepare to Establish Fujian Provincial Industrial Bank 82

Capital of One Million Already Raised

Fuzhou Correspondence: The Department of Finance hired Huang Qinshu, the eldest son of overseas Chinese Huang Yizhu, as the director of the preparatory office of the Industrial Bank this spring. However, due to various delays, preparations have only recently been completed. Huang sent his representative Huang Yishou to the province on the 18th to contact Luo Wang and other wealthy merchants to proceed with the establishment and find a location to build the bank's address in order to open as soon as possible. The bank's capital has now been raised to one million yuan. The nature of the bank is that of a limited liability company, with the purpose of regulating local finance and developing local industries. It is organized by commercial shareholders and submitted to the provincial government for approval and then reported to the Ministry of Finance for record. Its headquarters will be located in Xiamen, with a branch in Fuzhou. The business term is set at 20 years, and the shareholders' meeting may decide to extend it upon expiration. Its capital is divided into 10,000 shares, each share worth 100 yuan in national currency. Business will begin when 500,000 yuan in shares has been raised, and the remainder will be raised successively. The types of stocks are divided into five types: one share, five shares, ten shares, fifty shares, and one hundred shares. The right to buy and sell is limited to citizens of the Republic of China. The scope of business has also been determined to be six items: (i) Receiving various deposits and savings, (ii) Handling various remittances and trading in marketable securities, (iii) Managing the property and funds of public institutions or organizations, (iv) Establishing warehouses for mortgaged goods, (v) Handling industrial loans, (vi) Operating other banking businesses decided by the board of directors. Speculative business and the following matters are not allowed: 1. Purchasing or accepting stocks of various companies, 2. Purchasing stocks of this bank, using stocks of this bank as collateral for loans, 3. Unsecured loans and overdrafts without market value collateral, 4. Except for real estate necessary for business operations, trading is not allowed. The bank has 11 directors, who are elected by shareholders with 60 or more shares. There are three supervisors, one appointed by the Department of Finance, and the remaining two elected by the shareholders' meeting from shareholders with 20 or more shares. The headquarters has a president and a vice president, appointed by the board of directors, to preside over all bank affairs and execute the resolutions of the board of directors and shareholders' meeting. (December 22)

Investigation of Fisheries in Qinzhou, Guangdong 83

Externally Restricted by the French, Internally Oppressed by Heavy Taxes

Fishermen Adhere to Old Methods, Fisheries Are Declining Daily

Guangzhou Correspondence: Qinzhou in Guangdong is close to the southern frontier, facing the Gulf of Tonkin. In the past, marine products were abundant. However, recently, due to the lack of new methods for harvesting fish and the shortage of capital, large-scale fishing operations are impossible. Furthermore, local fishermen are burdened by heavy taxes, hindering their development. Even if they venture far offshore, they are restricted by the French territorial waters, controlled by foreigners. Therefore, in recent years, Qinzhou's fisheries have been declining daily, leading to increasingly difficult lives for fishermen. The Guangdong Provincial Department of Construction, in order to promote the local fisheries, recently sent specialists to investigate, to design a plan to revitalize the industry. The latest findings are as follows: ㈠ The location and depth of Qinzhou fishing port: The fishing port is commonly known as Yuchun Port, also called Longmen Port, located in Qinzhou Port, spanning Fangcheng, Qisha, and other places, including Longmen Port, Ganzhou, and the construction of "Daughter Trench."

Nanchang Correspondence: Banditry in Jiangxi Province is gradually being suppressed. To prevent the resurgence of the "Red Peril," the Ganzhou authorities have added trenches outside the city for defense. They have also ordered all men and women in the city between the ages of sixteen and fifty to work on the project. Officials from various agencies, teachers, faculty, and students from various schools must also form special teams to participate in the work for two weeks. Since the news spread, there has been no issue with the men. However, the women who are accustomed to pampering, especially educated female students, deeply worried about the heavy tasks. Principal Tan of the Provincial Second Girls' Middle School believed that this action related to bandit prevention and should not be delayed. Yesterday, she discussed with the school's physical education department and decided to lead over a hundred faculty, staff, students, and school workers with hoes and other farming tools to the designated location for trench construction. Although the delicate female students felt extremely tired, their spirits were high, forgetting their hardships. The county's various sectors praised the move. In the future, after the trench is completed, it will be called "Daughter Trench," so that the elegant name of "Lady City" will no longer be unique (Shen Shi News Agency).

Sanlian Bay, West Ring, Butterfly Ridge, Longmen Port has a depth of four to ten fathoms, the bottom being rocky, rich in oysters. Sanlian Bay has a depth between four and six fathoms, the bottom being a mixture of sand and stone, yielding few fish. West Ring has a depth of five to eight fathoms, and Butterfly Ridge has a depth of six to nine fathoms, where fish are becoming scarce. ㈡ Fishery production and fishing boats: Longmen Bay produces oysters; Sanlian Bay, West Ring, and Butterfly Ridge produce red fish, sardinella, dried fish, goby fish, and shrimp. There are about one hundred and fifty to three hundred large and small fishing boats distributed in the above three areas. ㈢ Fishing season and quantity: The fishing season is in the four months of August, September, October, and November. Spring is the off-season, and April, May, June, and July are rest days. Large fishing boats catch about 35,000 catties per season per pair of boats. However, the number of large fishing boats in the entire port is less than twenty. Medium-sized boats catch about 26,000 catties per season per pair of boats. Small fishing boats are more numerous than medium-sized boats, with each small boat catching about 5,000 to 6,000 catties per season. Longmen Port produces about 40,000 catties of oysters annually. ㈣ Fish trade and price: The fish caught by fishermen are concentrated in the fish markets in Beihai Port. The fish markets pay according to market prices and specialize in wholesale. Ordinary fish varieties cost about nine to ten yuan per hundred catties. Oysters cost eighty yuan per hundred catties, and eels cost one hundred and twenty yuan per hundred catties. ㈤ Heavy customs duties: Every fishing boat entering the port through the Beihai Customs must pay a tax of one hundred yuan, or they will be detained. Fishermen have no way to complain. ㈥ The issue of fishing in the sea: As soon as the large and small fishing boats sail to Dongxing Fangcheng for fishing, they are often unreasonably arrested by the Vietnamese French authorities, who consider it to be fishing across the border, and the fines are very harsh. If they cannot pay, the fishing boats will be confiscated, and the fishermen will be imprisoned. Therefore, fishermen now hope that the government will delineate the territorial waters as soon as possible, establish water boundaries, and maintain our territorial sea rights. ㈦ Fishermen's livelihood: Qinzhou fishermen live a very hard life. Recently, due to the increasing cost of living, expensive fishing gear, heavy internal tax burden, and external constraints by the French, they work hard all year round but can only barely make ends meet, with no profit to speak of. If they cannot cope, they will inevitably sell their children and boats to pay off debts. This kind of situation is common throughout the year. (December 23rd)

Ge Guangting Talks About the Recent Situation of the Jiaoji Railway 84

Short Revenue in July, August, and September, Gradually Better After October

Construction of Boshan Branch Line Still Stalled

Jinan Correspondence: Ge Guangting, Chairman of the Jiaoji Railway, accompanied Shen Honglie from Qingdao to Ji yesterday. That night, he sent Shen and Han Fuqu to Beiping. Ge stayed in Jinan due to business and is scheduled to return to Qingdao tonight (24th). I visited Ge and inquired about the railway's business situation this year. Ge said that the railway's operating revenue was originally budgeted at 17.3 million yuan for the 21st year. However, the business was poor in July, August, and September (due to the flooding in Boshan, various mines were flooded, and the sales of coal were hindered by Japanese coal), resulting in a major impact. Revenue was only 700,000 yuan in July, 800,000 yuan in August, and 900,000 yuan in September. It was not until October that there was a slight improvement. November revenue was 1.5 million yuan. It is estimated that 15 million yuan can still be collected by next June. During the business decline this summer, tightening measures were implemented. Orders were issued to suspend promotions and salary increases (about 110,000 yuan per year). The road administration's public car expenses (about 30,000 yuan per year) were also cancelled, and subsidies for Jiaotong University interns (8,000 yuan per year) were stopped to maintain operations. Now that revenue is better, it is planned to restore everything to its original state from January next year. Because railways are a business, tightening measures are implemented when revenue is low, and expansion is carried out when revenue is high. The minimum requirement is to match revenue and expenses without surplus. It must not be allowed to accumulate debt and lose money. The coal transport from Zichuan and Boshan has now recovered partially. The issue of purchasing the Boshan light railway to build a branch line of this railway is still stalled. The Japanese debt interest is 2.4 million yuan. The first half's 1.2 million yuan has been paid, and the second half's 1.2 million yuan can also be paid off by the end of this month. Preparations for redeeming the railway are currently underway. The railway owes 40 million yuan in Japanese debt. Although the railway has not been redeemed in ten years, the assets have been increasing continuously, now reaching 30 million yuan, which is better than other railways. (December 24th)

Second Day of the Jiangsu Provincial Assembly 85

The Third Jiangsu Provincial Assembly held a memorial service for the Premier at 8:00 a.m. today (26th). The preliminary meeting was held at 2:00 p.m. Zhou Shaocheng chaired the meeting. After the ceremony, the chairman reported the nominations for: ㈠ Five members of the Presidium, besides Gu Ziyang and Zhou Shaocheng, who have already been nominated by the Provincial Executive Committee, the remaining three should be elected by the representatives. ㈡ Seven members of the Proposal Review Committee. ㈢ Five members of the Resolution Sorting Committee. ㈣ Three members of the Declaration Drafting Committee. ㈤ Eleven special committee members. After the report, designated staff began distributing ballots. The three members of the Presidium were elected first, and the results are as follows: Xu Yongji, 111 votes; Cao Bingqian, 85 votes; Sheng Xiru, 78 votes.

Songjiang People Request Exemption from Converting Cropland to Paddy Field 86

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance is handling the case of converting cropland to paddy field. Due to the lack of understanding of the actual situation of the cropland and closed-door policy making, there are many obstacles. Therefore, the old Songjiang-affiliated counties of Fengxian, Jinshan, etc., find it difficult to implement, and it has been shelved until now. Only the former Finance Bureau of Songjiang County is eager to claim credit and seriously implemented it. However, in the past levies, the landowners believed that the cropland was of poor quality and cheap, and the taxes levied had exceeded 2% of the market value of the land. They could not bear any more burden. Therefore, this grain tribute actually remains in the hands of the clerks and the land guarantors. This is because the landowners are unable to pay. Currently, local people believe that the provincial authorities may not understand the actual situation and have been misled by the county bureau. They have appointed Li Kan and others as representatives to go to Beijing and the province to explain the differences between cropland and paddy field: ㈠ Difference in soil quality: The paddy field in Songjiang is in the hinterland and of better quality, while the cropland, except for a few scattered areas, has different characteristics or can be increased appropriately. The rest are all coastal, so the soil is mostly sandy and contains salt, which is not suitable for planting. ㈡ Difference in terrain: The terrain of Songjiang is high in the south and low in the north. The paddy fields are all in the north, so water is easily irrigated and planting is light. The cropland is all in the south, so water is difficult to irrigate and planting is heavy. Farmers raise an ox, and the strength of the ox is equal. In the cropland, only ten acres can be planted, while in the paddy field, dozens of acres can be planted. Some do not even need the ox's power and replace it with manual labor. ㈢ Difference in area: During the land survey in the Qing Dynasty, the paddy field was six bow (unit of measurement), and the cropland was five bow. Therefore, the area of the paddy field is large, and the area of the cropland is small. ㈣ Difference in rent: The paddy field is from 1.2 to 1.4 dou per mu, while the cropland is all below 1 shi, even only 3 or 4 dou. On average, it is no more than 6 dou. ㈤ Difference in planting: The paddy field is planted with rice, while the cropland can only be planted with cotton, or only with miscellaneous grains or sweet potatoes and other cheap things. Even if rice is planted reluctantly, the yield is very different (in an average year, the paddy field can harvest more than 2 shi of rice per mu, while the cropland only harvests about 1 shi per mu, and some do not even reach 1 shi). ㈥ Difference in value: People buy and sell land based on the rent amount, not based on mu. The same mu can be sold for 1 shi in the paddy field, while in the cropland it can only be sold for 3, 5, or 7 or 8 dou. Moreover, the paddy field in Pubei is more expensive, while the cropland in Punan is cheaper. The government's reorganization of land tax should be a whole plan, not piecemeal, which leads to many disturbances. Songjiang County is currently ordered to conduct a land survey. It seems that the conversion of cropland to paddy field should be temporarily suspended until the land survey is completed, a unified overview of the situation can be had, the land tax can be averaged to ensure fairness and convenience of implementation. It is hoped that the county bureau will be ordered to temporarily suspend the conversion of cropland to paddy field. At the same time, the deadline for the land survey should be limited, and the coastal cropland should be processed ahead of schedule to clarify the situation. It is believed that the provincial authorities will cherish the people's livelihood and will be happy to accept this.

It was resolved that the district should temporarily advance the funds before the security expenses are collected. ㈠ Regarding the 3,000 yuan for the security training class in this county, which was previously borrowed from the Bureau of Finance and Property, how should it be repaid? Resolution of the Strike at Yanqiao 89

The 13th branch bureau chief of the fifth district Yanqiao town's public security was due to the indiscriminate arrest of villagers, the incident caused a town wide strike, as was reported by this newspaper, yesterday the County Public Security Bureau Chief Wu Dexin, because the strike was long and unresolved, affecting the local public safety, therefore he dispatched the first public security bureau chief Gao Chongshan, accompanied by supervisors Yao Lemin and the business group of captains of the roving team Huang Shuying, etc, went down to the countryside to mediate, persuaded people to resume work, after Gao arrived in the countryside, first at the Fifth District public offices, convening the district chief, town chief, deputy, etc, to open a talk, discuss ways to persuade a resumption of work, followed by a journey to the people's teahouse, summoning the merchants and villagers to persuade a return to work, When Gao and others were responsible for returning to the city and reporting to the Public Security Bureau's decision to replace Zhang Xin, all merchants and civilians began setting off firecrackers at about 3 pm, and the whole town resumed business, after the matter, and also with the town chief Fan Hengbo, taking the lead in place of the provincial government, requesting quick orders to the county, to investigate the matter.

An Elderly Woman Killed by Robbers 90

In the Nianqi Seventh Township of the Fourteenth District (Kaihua Township), Upper Cai Lane, there lived an elderly woman named Wang Xu, nearly sixty years old. She had three sons: Gui Xing, Ju Jin, and Shi Qing, all of whom were adults. Gui Xing and Shi Qing worked as blacksmiths in Shanghai, while Ju Jin was a soldier far away. Xu was frugal and had some savings, but unexpectedly she was targeted by robbers. On the night of the winter solstice, she was suddenly strangled to death. The next day, neighbors saw that Xu had not opened her door for a long time and became suspicious. They climbed over the wall to investigate and found Xu lying stiff on the bed. They sent someone to Shanghai to report to her son. Gui Xing and others returned and broke down the door. They saw five finger marks on Xu's face, rope marks on her neck, and blood flowing from her ears, eyes, mouth, and nose. The clothes and ornaments in the box had been looted.

Multiple Robberies on Land and Water 91

Shi Jinzhang, a well-off villager from Shixiang Shang Township in the Fourteenth District, loaded twelve large pigs and several shi of rice and wheat to sell in Zhejiang. He earned more than 300 yuan and was returning home by boat. However, while passing through Taihu Lake, a net boat suddenly appeared, and six robbers jumped out, swarming the boat. They looted all the 300 yuan and stabbed Shi's thighs and arms with sharp knives, causing injuries. In addition, Zhang Longxiao's family in Xiaozhang Lane, Yangming West Township in the Third District, was also raided by six or seven robbers at about 2 a.m. yesterday. They looted gold rings, cash, clothes, etc., with a total loss of about 500 yuan. Furthermore, the homes of Dong Shuhe, the town chief of Ge Di Bridge, and the Rong family in Dadong Lane, Yucun Township, were also robbed on the previous night, with losses of two to three hundred yuan.

Chen Shaokuan Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday 103

Replenishing the Navy is Not Easy to Achieve

The Fuhai Incident Has Been Explained

Navy Minister Chen Shaokuan arrived in Shanghai by night train from Nanjing yesterday morning and immediately changed to a car and went to see Chairman Chiang Kai-shek on Jiaer Ye Ai Road. After talking for about 20 minutes, he went to visit President Song at Qiqi Road and returned to the Jiangnan Shipyard in Gaochang Temple at 11 o'clock to rest. Central News Agency reporters visited Minister Chen at the Jiangnan Shipyard yesterday afternoon to inquire about his opinions on replenishing the Navy and the shooting incident on the Fuhai patrol ship. According to Minister Chen, the Third Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee discussed the issue of replenishing the Navy. However, the situation of the Navy is different from that of the Army and Air Force. The Army can recruit soldiers today and form a division tomorrow, and the Air Force can raise 1 million yuan and purchase dozens of aircraft. As for replenishing the Navy, it is not as easy as the Army and Air Force. The cost of warships and submarines is hundreds of thousands of yuan for each small ship, and millions to tens of millions of yuan for each large ship. It is not enough to have three or five ships. At a time when the national treasury is not well off, where can such a large sum of money come from to replenish the Navy? Therefore, although the Navy Department has long had a plan to expand the Navy, it is constrained by economics and cannot be realized. Although the Third Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee discussed the case of replenishing the Navy, it is likely that the reality will not be as easy to achieve as the ideal. The shooting incident on the Fuhai patrol ship of the Jiangzhe Fisheries Administration was due to a misunderstanding and has now been explained. The Ministry of Industry has agreed to allocate the cost of the ship owed to the Jiangnan Shipyard. The Navy Department's Hai Ning ship was originally scheduled to go to Songkou for a test run today (yesterday), but due to bad weather, it has been postponed to the 30th. The Hai Ning ship's test firing results were very good and has now been stationed in Fuzhou. There are warships stationed and patrolling along the Yangtze River, so the water surface is quite calm.

City Chamber of Commerce to Discuss This Year's Final Tax Collection Date Tomorrow 104

Hankou Set for January 24th

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce has received a letter from the Hankou Municipal Chamber of Commerce stating that the city has set January 24th of the 22nd year of the Republic (1933) as the final deadline for final tax collection, which is also the Lunar New Year's Eve. Given the close business ties between Shanghai and Hankou, the chamber needs to discuss how Shanghai should proceed, considering Hankou's regulations. Therefore, it was decided at the 22nd Executive Committee meeting to convene a joint meeting of executive and supervisory members tomorrow (Wednesday) at 4 PM to discuss the matter together. A notice has already been issued.

New Fu Tai Ship Runs Aground Outside Wusong Mouth and Sinks 107

Thirty Crew Members Fortunately Rescued

Total Losses Estimated at 300,000 Yuan

The New Fu Tai vessel, owned by the Shanghai Heping Shipping Company, encountered fog and ran aground outside the Wusong Mouth yesterday morning, sinking. The ship's hull was damaged, and efforts are underway to salvage it. The details are as follows:

Circumstances of the Accident 108

The New Fu Tai vessel departed from Pukou on the 23rd of this month, carrying 4,000 tons of Zhongxing coal, destined for Ningbo for delivery. At 4:45 AM yesterday, the ship was in the Litongsha waters, located at 122 degrees 10 minutes east longitude and 30 degrees 43 minutes north latitude. At that time, there was heavy fog at sea, and the driver mistakenly entered the navigation route, hitting a submerged reef. The third compartment was severely hit with a large hole.

Ship Owner's Telegram 109

After the accident, the ship owner, a Polish national named Kszeminski, urgently sent a wireless telegram for help. The third compartment was already flooded, and because it was heavily loaded, it sank further after the water entered, making the situation very dangerous.

Japanese Ship Assists in Rescue 110

The Hakone Maru, a European liner of the Japanese Mail Steamship Company, was en route from Hong Kong to Shanghai and passed through the Tongsha waters. After receiving the New Fu Tai vessel's distress signal, it sailed to the site of the accident to assist in the rescue. According to a telegram sent to Shanghai by the Hakone Maru on behalf of the New Fu Tai, not only was the third compartment flooded, but the engine room was also flooded, and the situation was extremely dangerous.

Shanghai Office Inquires 111

After receiving the news, this reporter went to the company to inquire. According to its manager, Qian Fulin, after receiving the telegram about the accident, the Shanghai office sent a wireless telegram to the ship owner, Kszeminski, to inquire, but has not yet received a reply. What is known at present is that after the ship accident, a Japanese ship and a pilot boat from Tongsha were assisting in the rescue. The ship has gone missing. Fortunately, all thirty crew members and sailors can be rescued.

Ship Sinks 112

When the rescue ship Tongshun arrived at Tongsha, the New Fu Tai vessel had already sunk into the sea. The masts, chimneys, and pilot platform could still be seen above the water during low tide, but the lifeboats were not found. All crew members from the shipowner down have been rescued and will take the ship to Shanghai. The rescue ship is currently sounding its horn frequently in the waters near the sunken ship to search for the lifeboats.

Amount of Losses 113

The New Fu Tai vessel had a load of 4,000 tons. This time, the sinking, combined with the Zhongxing coal carried and the public and private items of the crew and sailors, is estimated to result in a total loss of over 300,000 yuan.

China National Aviation Corporation Missing Plane Safe 114

Landed Due to Fog, Discovered Yesterday

Passengers Safe, Mail Delivered to Post Office

The China National Aviation Corporation's flight to Hankou, which took off at 8 AM on the 25th, went missing mid-flight due to heavy fog and lack of visibility. The company immediately dispatched business director Nie Kaiyi and pilot Anderson in an amphibious aircraft to search along the original route. However, after the aircraft took off, the company suddenly received a telegram from Nanjing at around 11 AM stating that the missing aircraft had been found about 30 miles from Nanjing. According to reports, the aircraft has a carrying capacity of 1,200 pounds and can accommodate six people. After the aircraft was discovered at the Nanjing station, a large car was immediately hired to go to the accident site and pick up the mail and passengers to Nanjing. Because the aircraft landed automatically at the time, the passengers and the aircraft were not damaged. This reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency visited the company's secretary, Li Diezhuang, yesterday. According to him, the matter went well. A telegram has been received from Nanjing reporting safety. The company's Deputy Director Nie and pilot Anderson have also gone to Nanjing and will return to Shanghai within days. Last Saturday's flight from Shanghai to Beijing was also cancelled four times due to poor weather. Therefore, the mail was immediately sent to the post office to be transported to Beijing by train that day.

The Department of Industry and the Navy Jointly Resolve the Fuhai Frigate Gunfire Incident 119

Audit Unit Re-Examines Repair Costs

Captain Guo Wei Has Resigned to Take Responsibility

Datong News Agency reports that the misunderstanding between the Fuhai patrol frigate of the Fisheries Bureau and the Navy has been resolved peacefully through negotiations between Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo and Minister of the Navy Chen Shaokuan. The details are as follows:

Resolution in Beijing: After the incident occurred, Zhou Bingkui, the acting director of the Fisheries Bureau, immediately telegraphed Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industry in Nanjing for a decision. Chen believed that although the matter concerned the repair costs of the Fuhai patrol frigate, it was essentially a matter between the Ministry of Industry and the Ministry of the Navy. Therefore, he negotiated with Minister of the Navy Chen Shaokuan in Beijing. Both agreed that during the national crisis, there should be no more misunderstandings and were willing to reconcile. In addition to the Ministry of Industry compensating the Jiangnan Shipyard for the repair costs, the Navy Department decided not to pursue the gunfire incident further.

Review of Repair Costs: According to the Jiangnan Shipyard, the Fuhai frigate owed more than 20,000 taels in repair costs. According to the Fisheries Bureau, the Fuhai frigate owed only 7,000 or 8,000 taels, a significant difference between the two sides. At that time, the Fuhai frigate was entrusted to the Jiangnan Shipyard for repairs when Kong Xiangxi was the Minister of Industry and Han Yougang was the Director of the Fisheries Bureau. Several years have passed, making it difficult to verify. Chen Gongbo has now ordered the audit unit of the Ministry of Industry to review the costs. Once the review is completed, the Finance Department will be consulted to transfer the funds to the Navy Department to complete the payment procedures.

Captain Resigns: After this incident occurred, Guo Wei, the captain of the Fuhai frigate, submitted his resignation to the Fisheries Bureau on the 22nd to take responsibility. Zhou Bingkui, the acting director of the Fisheries Bureau, immediately forwarded the resignation to the Minister of Industry for approval. The decision of the Ministry of Industry is still pending.

The Repair Process of the Difficult Project on the Northern Jiangsu Canal 122

Laisheng'an Breach

Xinsheng News Agency: Last August, a major flood caused disaster, and dozens of counties on both sides of the Northern Jiangsu Canal became ponds. The eastern side of the canal suffered the most severe damage. Therefore, the canal's dikes are purely for protecting the eastern bank. The purpose of setting up the western dike is to protect the eastern dike so that the waters of the Baoying, Gaoyou, and Shaobo lakes do not directly impact the eastern dike. The eastern dike is the protection of dozens of counties downstream. Last year, there were twenty-seven breaches in the eastern dike. It was difficult to close and repair the breaches. Among them, the Laisheng'an breach, ten miles north of Shaobo Town, was the most troublesome. After the breach was closed, there were two more collapses and one external slope slippage. Many contractors and technicians were imprisoned. The Jiangsu Provincial Government also sold Han Guojun, the director of the Northern Jiangsu Canal Project Rehabilitation Committee, to compensate for the repairs. After Xu Ji, the section chief and technician of the Department of Construction, surveyed it, he designed to separate the silt with stone tanks, and it was completed the day before yesterday. On the 23rd, a Xinsheng News Agency reporter, along with Zhang Junsheng, a technician from the Department of Construction, Wang Zizun, the director of the Jiangdu section of the Northern Jiangsu Canal Engineering Bureau, and technician Mao Feng, went north from Yangzhou along the canal to inspect this famous Huai project and asked about the evolution of the canal management funds. The following is a record:

(Zhaoguan Dam and Its Breach) The reporter and others went north from Shaobo and first arrived at Zhaoguan Dam. The dam is more than forty zhang long. Last year, the question of opening the dam caused a major dispute. This place was originally one of the Guihai Dams. After the dam was opened in the nineteenth year of Daoguang in the Qing Dynasty, it took more than four years and countless expenses, and many people died before it was completed. Because the place had previously breached, the bottom of the dam was very deep, and the foundation was not strong. After the repair, the Jiangsu governor奏准was approved to never open the dam. During the flood, the people in Yunxi demanded the opening of the dam, surrounding the directors of the Canal Engineering Bureau, Zhang Jian and Han Guojun, in Gaoyou. At that time, the Jiangsu provincial officials were also persuaded by the theory of Guihai. After Zhang Han went to Yundong for investigation, they believed that it was impossible to open it and insisted on not allowing it. It was the same last year. Later, a breach of more than thirty zhang in length occurred north of Zhaoguan Dam. When closing and repairing the breach, the main engineer had proposed to dig up the dam to hold clear silt, because the embankment slope contained silt, but black soil was found at the base of the slope. (Black soil is silt that contains moisture and has no adhesion, making it difficult to bond with other soil and rock.) Technician Xu believed that the amount of silt was limited, and since there was already a way out, it might as well increase the embankment and press it out before it was completed. Because the foundation of the Zhaoguan Dam was not solid, it was three feet lower than the embankment. Increasing the height would cause it to sink. This happened repeatedly, and then the stones from the four terraces of the embankment slope were moved to the three terraces before the dam could be balanced. Now it is the same height as the embankment.

(Three Collapses at Laisheng'an) Laisheng'an is ten miles north of Zhaoguan Dam and three miles south of Lujin Town. The breach is thirty-six zhang long. The first time, a construction company contracted to complete it for 60,000 yuan. When it was about to close, it suddenly collapsed again. The contractor was imprisoned in Jiangdu County. The second time was in March of this year. The breach had been repaired. When dismantling the river dams at both ends, the embankment suddenly collapsed again, and the two engineers in charge of the section were also imprisoned in Jiangdu. The third time was in September of this year. The river dams at both ends had been dismantled, and the outer slope had slipped and the top had sunk five feet. The Yangzhou office of the Canal Engineering Rehabilitation Committee drafted three kinds of remedies, with costs of more than 60,000 yuan for type A, more than 40,000 yuan for type B, and more than 10,000 yuan for type C. The Jiangsu Provincial Government telegraphed Han Guojun, the director of the association, demanding that he compensate for the repairs. Han agreed to return to his hometown to sell his property to supplement the embankment repairs. Later, Xu Ji, the section chief of the Construction Department, investigated the site for three days and conducted detailed research. He believed that the cause of the slippage was (1) the sweeping work was not strong enough to withstand the soil pressure and moved outward, and (2) the silt at the bottom of the river could not withstand the soil pressure and retreated and arched upward, causing the embankment slope to sink. The remedies were only two kinds: sinking rows and filling pits. However, the sinking row project was time-consuming, labor-intensive, and costly, and its location was appropriate for the accumulation of rocks in the heart of the river, which would inevitably be dangerous for future ship traffic. Therefore, he changed to the latter method and added a layer of soil curtain to the slope to repair the sweeping work.

(Xu Ji Talks About the Difficult Canal Project) On the 24th, Xu Ji, the section chief and technician of the Zhenjiang Construction Department, Xu's given name is Decheng, a native of Nantong, is rich in water conservancy engineering experience. He has invented several kinds of water conservancy surveying instruments and engineering methods. Last year, most of the difficult projects on the Northern Jiangsu Canal were designed and resolved by him. Xu talked to me (Xu said that he had traveled around the world to investigate water conservancy, and felt that although each had its strengths and weaknesses, the old Chinese method was the best in comparison. When I tell people this, I am often ridiculed for being pedantic, but the facts are so and cannot be ignored. Last year, the largest breach in the eastern dike of the canal was the restoration of Dangjunlou. I mainly used the sinking row method, using stones to press the purple row to sink, and on one side, the weight of the stones was used to balance the soil pressure. On one side, the water leakage effect of the row was used to reduce the moisture in the silt before it was completed. However, some technical personnel still advocated trying the method of building with stones. As a result, more than 1.3 million yuan was spent, but it still collapsed and was eventually replaced with the old sinking row method.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Inland River Machinery Factory Reorganized and Resumed Work 123

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Inland River Machinery Factory has been closed for a long time. The Shanghai No. 1 Cotton Mill Labor Dispute Still Unresolved After Mediation by the Social Affairs Bureau 128

Management Decides to Continue Suspending the Night Shift

The Labor Union to Hold a General Meeting Today to Discuss

The Shanghai No. 1 Cotton Mill in Zhoujiaqiao, due to sluggish business, decided to suspend the night shift in the weaving room, starting with Group 111 on December 8th, resulting in the unemployment of over 200 workers. The more than 1,000 workers on the entire night shift were in a state of panic. Despite repeated mediation by party and government agencies, no resolution was reached. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau formally convened a Labor-Management Mediation Committee to mediate according to law. Attending committee members included Tang Menghong and Wen Xirong from management, Fan Luquan and Sun Shouxing from the labor side, and Lu Yinchu from the Municipal Party Headquarters. Zhu Guilin, Chairman of the Social Affairs Bureau, presided, and Wang Zuofang served as the recorder. Representatives from each group of workers were also present. The management stated that business continued to be poor and that the remaining groups on the night shift, Groups 222 and 333, would inevitably be suspended by January of the 22nd year at the latest. The labor side argued that if all three groups were suspended, more than 1,000 workers would be unemployed and requested a postponement to avoid a labor strike. Regarding the suspension of Group 111, both sides agreed to change it to a rotating work system, with the original situation to be restored if business improved. Subsequently, discussions on calculating workers' wages on a monthly basis and the continued suspension of the other two night shift groups were postponed, as the labor side felt that the matter was significant and needed to be approved by a general meeting before a decision could be made. As a result, no agreement was reached. The Chairman announced that mediation would resume at 9:00 AM on the 28th, and the meeting adjourned at noon.

The 10th District Cotton Textile Industry Labor Union has scheduled a representative meeting for 1:00 PM today to discuss the approach. It has already reported to the Public Security Bureau and requested police protection. The Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau will send representatives to provide guidance.

The Jiangsu High Court Again Rules the Labor Side Not Guilty in the Case of the Female Worker Killed at the Yongan Factory 129

The Labor Union Petitions to Resolve the Outstanding Case

Party and Government Agencies Confer and Review

Last year, the Yongan No. 2 Yarn Factory in Wusong's Yunzaobang had excellent business, earning over 2 million yuan. The workers requested bonuses, but the factory refused, leading to a labor strike. On the evening of December 20th last year, the factory suddenly closed its doors, refusing to allow the night shift workers to enter. The factory's hired police opened fire, killing one female worker, Jiao Lianying, on the spot, and arresting twelve workers. After investigation by the Shanghai District Court, the arrested workers were found not guilty. The prosecutor, dissatisfied, appealed to the Jiangsu High Court. A year has passed, and the court has finally reached a verdict, again finding the workers not guilty. However, three of the arrested workers died of illness while in custody during the trial, a truly tragic situation. The labor-management dispute remains unresolved to this day. Now that the Songhu Incident has concluded, the 8th District Cotton Textile Industry Labor Union feels that the outstanding case should be resolved and has brought up the old case again, requesting five items: 1) Four months of bonuses for the 20th year, totaling over 400,000 yuan according to regulations, to be distributed equally among the factory's 7,000+ workers; 2) Payment of wages for statutory revolutionary holidays in the 20th year; 3) Reinstatement of all workers dismissed without cause; 4) Strict orders for the factory to fulfill the labor-management agreement, as management has violated it; 5) Compensation from management for deceased and injured workers. Yesterday, the union sent representatives Shen Yongming, Jin Yaowen, Zhao Rongsheng, and Wang Yuncheng to petition the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau. Li Weixiong from the Municipal Party Headquarters and Wang Bing from the Social Affairs Bureau received them and promised to confer with party and government agencies before reviewing the requests.

Anhui Huai River Improvement Association Seeks Opinions 130

The Anhui Huai River Improvement Association sent official letters to the governments, chambers of commerce, agricultural associations, education bureaus, and finance bureaus of counties along the Huai River, such as Huaihai, Zhenjiang in Jiangsu Province, Fengyang, Yingzhou, Sixian in Anhui Province, and counties in eastern Henan and southern Shandong. The letter stated, "Respected Sirs, the Huai River improvement issue concerns the interests of counties along the main and tributary streams of the Huai River in Jiangsu, Anhui, Shandong, and Henan provinces. Without a comprehensive plan, it is impossible to consider the overall situation. The Association's mission is to jointly advise and suggest to the government on the one hand, and to promote the autonomous organization and expression of opinions by the counties on the other, so that the Huai River improvement project can be implemented as soon as possible, thus permanently eliminating disasters, increasing production, and bringing deep benefits to the country and its people. Attached are a Huai River improvement proposal and a letter to fellow countrymen in each county. We respectfully hope that you will consider them sympathetically. We would be most grateful for your guidance." The letter also noted that the aforementioned proposal and letter to fellow countrymen can be obtained from the Association at No. 134, Pobo Fang, Luban Road, this city.

Japanese Ships Highly Active in China 131

Monopolizing Shipping Rights in the Northeast: The Dalian Steamship Company's Changchun Maru, one of its newly built first-class passenger ships, ran aground and capsized outside Yantai Port during a storm last summer. The Dalian Steamship Company entrusted the Tokyo Imperial Salvage Company to salvage the ship, which took a month to complete. The damage was enormous. After being towed to Japan for major repairs, including repairing the holes and rebuilding the passenger cabins, it has now been fully completed. The company has now obtained exclusive shipping rights in the Northeast, monopolizing almost all shipping routes from Yingkou, Andong, Dalian, and other ports to various Chinese seaports. Therefore, the Changchun Maru has resumed sailing to Shanghai on January 4th and will return to the Northeast. At the same time, to handle the abundance of North China cargo, the company has dispatched the Liaoning River Maru and other ships to Tianjin.

Increasing Sailings to Rush Japanese Goods: Since the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, Russian goods have been selling rapidly in China, especially next spring. Japanese merchants are taking advantage of this time to rush their stockpiled goods to China in order to dump them. Recently, Nippon Yusen Kaisha (NYK) ships have been bringing inferior goods, with three ships arriving in Shanghai every week, carrying approximately 50,000 pieces. Another 55,000 pieces are scheduled to be loaded and shipped within the year. Kawasaki Kisen Kaisha (K Line) is also taking the opportunity to add special China-Japan routes, dispatching the No. 2 Daian Maru and other ships to rush large quantities of Japanese goods to China. In addition, there are many other temporary Japanese ships coming to Shanghai, with at least two ships arriving every day.

Sun Yuanliang, the Newly Appointed Commander of the 88th Division, to Marry Today 133

At the Lakes Society Auditorium Today at Noon

The Bride is Miss Wu Yahui, Daughter of Wu Xingya

Sun Yuanliang, the Commander of the 259th Brigade of the 87th Division of the 5th Army, participated in the anti-Japanese war during the Shanghai Incident. His troops fought bravely in the Miaohang Dachang area and achieved great merit. After the ceasefire, he was promoted to Deputy Commander of the 88th Division. Recently, the Central Government promoted Sun to the rank of full Commander and ordered him to be reassigned to the command of the 13th Army under General Qian Dajun, and transferred to Wuhan for rest and training.

It is now learned that Commander Sun arrived in Shanghai from his defense post the night before last. He is scheduled to hold his wedding ceremony with Miss Wu Yahui, daughter of Wu Xingya, Director of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, at the Lakes Society Auditorium on Beijing Road at 4:00 PM today. Mayor Wu Tiecheng has been specially invited to officiate the wedding. Qian Dajun and Wu Xingya will be the hosts for the bride and groom, respectively. The introducers will be Yang Hu, Director of the Municipal Security Bureau, and Zhu Shaoliang, the former Commander-in-Chief of the 8th Route Army. It is reported that Commander Sun will return to his defense post in Wuhan with his new wife tomorrow (the 28th) after the wedding today, and will hold an oath-taking ceremony for his inauguration as Commander on New Year's Day.

Sixty-Year-Old Woman Run Over and Killed by Car 134

Gu Shoushi, an old woman from Taicang, was 60 years old. She worked as a domestic helper for a certain family at No. 669 Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession. At 6:40 PM on the 23rd, she went out and was crossing the road from south to north in front of No. 673 Avenue Edward VII. A car, No. 1550, driven by Ding Guoji, a chauffeur from a certain car dealership at No. 355 Jiujiang Road, was traveling east to west and was unable to avoid her. She was knocked down, suffering head injuries, and immediately fell unconscious. A policeman recorded the license plate number and sent the injured person to Renji Hospital for treatment, while taking the driver to the police station to report to the head of the station for investigation. The old woman, due to her age and severe injuries, died at 10:00 PM on the 24th. The hospital notified the police station, who transported the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Morgue for an autopsy. Yesterday morning, the Traffic Department summoned the deceased's relative, Gu Abao, to the case and reported it to the Second Special District Court, requesting Prosecutor Deng to come to the morgue. The prosecutor confirmed that the deceased had died from head injuries sustained when struck by a car. After the autopsy, the prosecutor returned to the courthouse, questioned the defendant about the circumstances of the accident, and then ordered the body to be released to the family after they signed a guarantee. The defendant was returned to the custody of the Traffic Department for legal action.

A Ticket's Worth a Life 136

Yesterday afternoon, when a southbound 京沪 train arrived in Shanghai, there was a poor man, about thirty years old, wearing thin and ragged clothes in the fourth-class carriage. He was unable to afford a ticket and sneaked in. However, upon arriving at the North Station, the ticket inspectors routinely checked tickets. He was unable to pass this difficult hurdle. In a moment of desperation, as the train was crossing a dry bridge and still moving at considerable speed, he disregarded his life and jumped off mid-journey to avoid censure. Unfortunately, he landed headfirst on the ground, his skull striking a stone. His brain and blood splattered everywhere, and he immediately fell unconscious. He was sent to Renji Hospital for treatment, but it was too late and he died. Yesterday, the Police Department instructed 吉一图 headman Yan Liugen to report the case to the District Court for autopsy.

Dr. Li Ji Lectured Yesterday on Recent Archaeological Discoveries in Henan 140

And Exhibited Western Zhou Artifacts Excavated from Xun County

The Academia Sinica held its first public lecture yesterday morning at 10:00 AM at the Mingfu Library of the Science Society of China on Avenue Albert. The speaker was Dr. Li Ji, Director of the Archaeological Group of the Institute of History and Philology of the Academia Sinica. The topic of the lecture was Recent Archaeological Discoveries in Henan. He also displayed many Western Zhou artifacts excavated from Xun County. Cai Yuanpei, President of the Academia Sinica, Yang Quan, Vice President, and guests such as Ye Gongchuo were in attendance, along with an audience of over 300 people. The lecture concerned ancient Chinese culture. The text is recorded below.

The Archaeological Group's recent archaeological work in Henan is still centered in Anyang and Hu County, south of Anyang, described as follows:

(Anyang) This is the seventh excavation. The results of the first three excavations can be found in the Anyang Excavation Reports published by the Institute of History and Philology. The most recent four excavations have all involved discoveries related to Yin-Shang architecture. Yin-Shang architecture used rammed earth as its foundation. Currently, rectangular and square platforms have been discovered. The square platforms are made of pure yellow earth and have stone column foundations in front. Around the perimeter are several sets of complete pig bones, likely the site of Yin-Shang sacrifices. There are many such sites, and the Academia Sinica plans to continue excavating. In due course, a general outline of the Yin-Shang palace system should be obtained.

(Xun County) Excavation began in the spring of this year. There are many tombs from the Bronze Age in this area. They have been repeatedly looted and destroyed by local tyrants, ruffians, and antique dealers. Since the Archaeological Group began working here, eight tombs have been cleared, all of which have been looted, but still contain some remaining funerary objects, mostly chariot and horse decorations, as well as halberds, spears, axes, and other weapons. The most astonishing discovery is that these tombs often contain horses buried alive. Next to the tombs, horse pits were often built separately. The largest horse pit discovered contains the remains of over 60 horses, along with numerous chariot and horse decorations. The chariot decorations can be used to reconstruct a portion of the ancient war chariot system, which is a major recent contribution to the field of archaeology. There are still many unexcavated tombs of this type that have been looted. The Academia Sinica plans to continue clearing these tombs next spring, at which time new discoveries will be reported.

Ye Yuhu and Others Launch Ancient Collection Exhibition 141

Mr. Jin Youfei, owner of Youfei Zhai, a great collector from the Qing Dynasty, was obsessed with antiquities throughout his life. He amassed a rich collection of bronzes, steles, calligraphy and paintings by famous figures from the three dynasties, carvings, coral, jadeite, white jade, agate, as well as porcelain, lacquerware, and bamboo artifacts. Among them, Song Dynasty Ke Kiln, Fahua Glazed Beauty, and Song and Yuan Dynasty silk paintings are the most precious. Now, Ye Yuhu, Jiang Xingjie, Wang Wenxin, Ha Shaofu, and others have launched an exhibition at the Chen Ying Shi Memorial Hall at the intersection of Guizhou Road on Beijing Road, displaying the collection for one week. Gentlemen who love antiquities are welcome to visit and view the exhibition.

Deadline: End of This Month

There are 462 households in this city with self-installed water supply equipment who have registered and obtained licenses from the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau. Taxpayers' Association Sends Another Letter to the Public Works Department 145

Regarding the Telephone Price Increase

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession has sent another letter to the Director-General of the Public Works Department regarding the telephone price increase. The letter states: "To the Director-General: We received a letter from the First District Branch of the Shanghai Citizens' Federation and the Nanjing Road Business Federation, which included a reply from the Public Works Department in response to their letter of December 1st. The reply listed the Shanghai Telephone Company's losses over the years as justification for the telephone price increase. We hereby reply: The Public Works Department previously published an article in the newspapers on November 18th to defend the company regarding the telephone price increase. Our association has already strongly refuted this article. The department's reasons still favor the company and its biased view is excessive. Although the telephone company has incurred significant expenses due to the replacement of new equipment, according to its own statement, from the establishment of the company on August 5, 1930, to the end of September this year, a total of 26 months, the company has lost a total of 218,430 taels of silver. Even considering the losses over 26 months, the Shanghai Telephone Company, despite its efforts to expand its lines more than fourfold and employing mostly Westerners with high salaries, has suffered losses due to extravagance and miscalculation. This cannot be a sufficient reason for a substantial increase in prices and retroactive compensation. The only way to resolve the current situation and quell the unrest is for an impartial organization to appoint accounting experts to audit the accounts to determine whether the price increase is necessary and whether the amount of the increase is reasonable, in order to seek a fair solution. We hope you will not succumb to pressure and abandon your responsibility to sacrifice the interests of the majority. Furthermore, we have not yet received a reply to our association's letter to the Public Works Department on November 15th. We do not know why. We are including this information and hope that you will investigate. We have repeatedly requested that this case be submitted to the board of directors of your department for reconsideration. We believe that the above information can assist in resolving the case. Therefore, we are writing to you to request your investigation and hope to receive a reply soon so that the public will not have to wait in anticipation."

Three Restrictions on Shanghai West Business Rickshaws 146

Business rickshaws in Shanghai West have not been registered in this city and have been operating privately. The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau started inspecting them on November 15th. By the end of November, the number of inspected vehicles reached as many as 4,328, which is feared to be an oversupply. This has an impact on the livelihood of rickshaw pullers. The Public Utilities Bureau, the Finance Bureau, the Social Affairs Bureau, and the Public Security Bureau have jointly discussed three restrictions: (1) All rickshaws operating beyond the boundaries of the four districts of Fahua, Pusan, Caojing, and Zhenru, and operating in other districts of the city, will have their temporary operating permits and donation certificates revoked. (2) Assuming that the city increases the number of business rickshaws in the future, holding a temporary operating permit for Shanghai West will not give priority to obtaining a license plate, and the regulations at that time will still apply. (3) All those who fail to pay the donation within the monthly stipulated period will have their temporary operating permits and donation certificates revoked. It is learned that the above measures have been approved by the Municipal Government and will be announced jointly by the four bureaus for public information.

Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Yugui of the First Special Court summoned them for trial. The plaintiff, Quan Shaowu, was absent, and his lawyer appeared in court, stating that Quan had left Shanghai on official business and requested a four-week adjournment. The three defendants, Tan, etc., unanimously opposed, stating that Quan had already filed a complaint and should be present for cross-examination. He should not be absent without reason and should be withdrawn according to law. The defendants all have official duties and cannot be detained in another place for a long time. If the adjournment is approved, they requested an adjournment of six weeks to allow them to return to their hometowns. Judge Liu then granted the request and ordered an adjournment of six weeks for another hearing.

Municipal Zoo Adds Peacock Pavilion and Aviary 153

Construction is Relatively Difficult

Opening Before New Year's Day is Not Possible

The Municipal Zoo on Wenmiao Road in this city has been under construction since the bidding process and has been going on for four months. The first phase of the project was completed in early December. The second phase of the project, such as stacking artificial mountains, revetment of the pond bank, installation of water pipes and electric lights, and laying grass and planting trees, is also half completed. The unfinished part is currently in progress. In addition, due to factual needs, a peacock pavilion and an aviary have been added outside the scope of the previous two weeks of the project. The aviary is built on the edge of the pond, half on land and half in the water. The construction is more difficult. It is estimated that it will not be completed until the end of January next year. It is feared that it will not be able to open before New Year's Day.

Woman Commits Suicide Due to Frustration Over Her Inability to Breastfeed Her Child Caused by Gambling Addiction 154

The woman, surnamed Shen Wu, was from Tongzhou and was only 25 years old. Her husband, Shen Dianxi, was a foreman and was nearly 60 years old. Because his wife had no children for several years, he took Shen Wu as a concubine in the hope that she would bear him a son. The family lived at No. 206 Hua Ji Road. In April of this year, Shen Wu gave birth to twins, which made Shen very happy and treated her with even greater importance. However, recently, Shen Wu became addicted to gambling and was immersed in it all day long. All her money and jewelry were lost to gambling. Although her husband knew about it and tried to dissuade her, she remained addicted and unrepentant. The other night, while Shen Wu was feeding her child, the child suddenly cried incessantly. Shen Wu realized that her milk had dried up. She was filled with resentment and conceived the idea of ending her life. She secretly swallowed opium and committed suicide. Her husband discovered it and sent her to Guangren Hospital for treatment, but she died. The hospital reported it to the Huishan Police Station, which sent detectives to investigate. They took the body to the Philand Road Morgue. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court appointed Prosecutor Zhan Liangce to inspect the body, accompanied by Forensic Medical Secretary Wang Zuyi. They certified the body and took testimony from Shen Dianxi, the husband of the deceased. Shen Dianxi stated that the deceased was his concubine. Recently, she liked to gamble and did not listen to his advice, even neglecting the child. This time, she suddenly committed suicide because she had no milk to feed the child, and the child cried all night, causing her resentment. However, he did not quarrel with her. After receiving the testimony, Prosecutor Zhan ruled that the deceased, Shen Wu, was a woman who died from opium poisoning before her death. The body was handed over to her husband, Shen Dianxi, to claim the coffin and burial. The opium was taken to the hospital for incineration.

Ma Dunhe Hat Shop Accountant Repeatedly Embezzles Funds 155

Even Used His Guarantor's Name

Forged a 300-Yuan IOU

Wang Yaoting, the accountant of Ma Dunhe Hat Shop, had been employed for more than ten years. At first, he seemed loyal, but in recent years, his behavior suddenly changed. He was addicted to prostitution and gambling. His salary was not enough to cover his expenses, so he privately embezzled the store's funds and falsified accounts. The store owner, Ma Yizhong, discovered it this summer. After checking the accounts, it was found that as much as 13,500 yuan had been embezzled. Wang also felt that he could not face anyone, so he asked his original guarantor, Wang Defu, to mediate. Ma Yizhong did not want to pursue the matter in depth out of consideration for feelings and allowed him to continue in his original position. However, he later discovered that Wang had falsified a public record passbook for 400 taels. Ma Yizhong could no longer tolerate it and reported it to the police station according to law, filing a lawsuit for forgery and fraud. The First Special District Court sentenced Wang to four months in prison. However, the day after the defendant was imprisoned, Wang Yuji suddenly came to the hat shop with the passbook to withdraw 700 yuan in principal and interest. After checking the books, it was learned that the passbook was also forged by Wang. When the deposit was made, Wang Yaoting had already pocketed the money. However, the hat shop could not let the depositor lose his principal and interest, so the hat shop immediately paid the principal and interest. At the same time, the hat shop continued to check the accounts and found a forged 300-yuan IOU from Wang Fuji. Wang Fuji is Wang Yaoting's guarantor, Wang Deyu. This can truly be said to be repaying kindness with evil. Now, Ma Yizhong believes that Wang has committed numerous acts of embezzlement and that the original sentence is not enough to cover his guilt. Therefore, he hired a lawyer to file a complaint regarding the newly discovered two acts of embezzlement, requesting that the defendant be brought to justice and punished in accordance with Articles 224, 351, and 363 of the Criminal Law. Yesterday, Judge Qian held a hearing and brought the defendant from the Western Prison. After examining the evidence, he ordered a postponement for further questioning of witnesses and ordered the defendant to be returned to custody.
