Clerk Communication

How to Avenge an Old Friend? 234

Editor:

Enveloped in angry and indignant emotions, I begin to ask a serious question, requesting you to provide a suitable answer, and please publish it in your publication for public criticism. The following are the facts of the matter:

My deceased friend, Mr. Pan, was a tenacious and hardworking young man. He and I graduated from ×× Middle School last autumn. At that time, the flames of youth were burning; the prospects for the future were active. We looked down on everything and each carried our diplomas, striding out of school and beginning to attack this mysterious society. I apparently won, but Pan lost his job! During this long period of unemployment, Mr. Pan recognized the true face of this society. He was so pessimistic that he almost committed suicide!

Later, through a friend's introduction, he met Mr. Jia, who worked at ×× Foreign Company. Through Mr. Jia's introduction, Mr. Pan obtained a position as a small clerk at ×× Foreign Company. Mr. Jia had a very high position in this foreign company, and almost all the Chinese staff were under his management. At that time, when Mr. Pan entered this foreign company, the manager (a Westerner) set his monthly salary at thirty-five taels, but Mr. Jia, considering himself meritorious for the introduction, deducted twenty yuan from Mr. Pan's monthly salary as a reward for the introduction. At the same time, he ordered Mr. Pan not to disclose this secret. Mr. Pan, fearing his power, dared to be angry but dared not speak out. Mr. Jia, seeing that Mr. Pan could be bullied, gave Mr. Pan the busiest work, making him work from eight in the morning to seven in the evening before letting him go home, using this to show off his achievements in front of outsiders, to boast that he had recommended the right person.

Mr. Jia was good at making money. Not only did he exploit lower-level staff to enrich himself, but he also founded a night school for the purpose of making money in his spare time, and asked Mr. Pan to help teach in his night school every night, only reimbursing Mr. Pan five yuan per semester for transportation expenses. This was simply making him do his duty, because he only received eight cents a month for two hours of teaching work every day! Mr. Pan, fearing his power, could only endure and accept his exploitation!

Mr. Pan bore fourteen hours of strenuous work every day, operating like a cow or horse, and Mr. Pan's labor reward was almost completely exploited by Mr. Jia. Thus, a striving, promising, and vigorous young man was ground down to a state of exhaustion and listlessness!

This summer, I accidentally met Mr. Pan on the road, and I almost couldn't believe that my old friend, whom I had been separated from for only half a year, had become so shockingly thin. So he told me about his recent situation. I had no choice but to sigh. I advised him that he would rather lose his job than take care of his health. But Mr. Pan said sadly: "I have tasted the taste of unemployment, and perhaps unemployment is even more painful than being exploited!" We quietly parted in such helpless silence. Now, after several months of separation, I suddenly heard the bad news of Mr. Pan's death from former classmates. It is said that half of the disease that caused his death was due to overwork; the other half was due to depression in his heart!

The unexpected stimulus ignited a cavity of anger in me. I finally couldn't restrain my tense emotions and prepared to avenge Mr. Pan. But Mr. Pan was not shot to death by Mr. Jia, and I cannot file a legal lawsuit. Moreover, Mr. Pan is already dead. He has no evidence to support the grievances he suffered during his lifetime, and Mr. Jia is now also working as a lawyer. Obviously, I cannot use the law to punish him. I also considered using a negative method to expose Mr. Jia's privacy to damage his reputation, but the method is too despicable. I am unwilling to sacrifice my personality as a condition for avenging my old friend. I have been wandering like this for several months, and I still cannot find a way to avenge Mr. Pan. Smart editor, smart readers, please sympathize with this unjustly dead small clerk, stand on a just position, and give me a suitable answer.

Sincerely, Zhongjie December 21st

Editor's Note: After reading this sad and angry letter, we felt as if our hearts were burning, and we expressed the same sympathy and grief for Mr. Pan as Mr. Zhongjie. A promising young man like Mr. Pan was sacrificed in this bad environment by the shameless and selfish Mr. Jia!

But we should know: The occurrence of this kind of thing is the result of a bad social system. It's not just Mr. Pan who has been sacrificed in this bad environment; it's not just Mr. Jia who is a sinister person in society. Therefore, we believe that this is a problem of the whole society, and we should start from the root to seek the overall reform.

Mr. Pan has been sacrificed, and he cannot be resurrected! We feel that thinking for the living is more urgent than avenging the dead; therefore, for the shameless, selfish people like Mr. Jia, we should unanimously criticize them, not obey, not compromise, seek benefits for the entire group of people, and seek happiness for the entire society; with a spirit of fearlessness, strive forward; never give up, and must make this kind of scum of humanity disappear from society before we are done.

In addition to sympathy and grief, we still want to regret Mr. Pan, and have to regret Mr. Pan's wrong concept at the time. We believe that rather than submitting to preserve oneself and working like a dog all day long, suffering the oppression of shameless and selfish people to the point of death; why not jump out of the fire pit and would rather lose one's job and fight to the death with shameless and selfish people!

Our method of avenging Mr. Pan is to promote the reform of the social system, so that people like Mr. Jia have no place to live. As for the personal handling of Mr. Jia, although legal proceedings cannot be initiated due to "lack of evidence"; what's the harm in making his bad deeds public? This will not only eliminate the evil spirit in our hearts; it can also prevent those who approach him from being fooled by him again. How can this kind of chivalrous act be considered "despicable"? How can it "lose personality"?

The emotion of hating evil like an enemy made us say the above a lot; but let's calm down and study the cause of Mr. Pan's death.

According to the letter, Mr. Pan died because of "accumulated labor becoming a disease" and "depression in his heart." This kind of cause is the most common in society. There are also two ways to solve it: ㈠ is to be optimistic in everything: No matter how busy the work is, no matter how difficult the environment is, always deal with it with an optimistic attitude. ㈡ is to pay attention to physical education; regarding this point, we have already said roughly in the article "Running into the Store and Ruining Your Body" in this column on the 24th of this month, readers can refer to it. We believe that if these two points can be implemented, then there will naturally be no depression in the heart, and accumulated labor will not become a disease.

Dear readers: After reading the above facts, what do you think? Is there a better way to deal with people like Mr. Jia? Is there a concrete plan for reforming the social system? I hope everyone will study it and express their great views.

Novel

Sympathizers (Continued Sixth) 235

— Zhang Henshui

"People like you should be liberated first." Wang Lao'er put his pipe in his mouth, stared at him with wide eyes, and said, "What, build a house?

? We till other people's fields, so naturally we have the landlord's house to live in, what's the point of building a house? I wouldn't build a house even if I had money. As the saying goes, 'If you don't get along with people, advise them to raise geese, if you don't get along with people, advise them to build houses.'" Meng Guobao didn't expect that what he was talking about was so far away from what he had expected, so he smiled and said, "I don't mean that." As he said that, he walked into the house with him. Wang Lao'er's house was five rooms, half tile and half grass. The central hall was thatched roofed. The grass heads under the eaves were like the silk tassels of a glass lamp. Such eaves surrounded a square courtyard of five feet on all sides. Naturally, it seemed that the courtyard was too big. A big spider web was hung in the corner of the house. In the hall, a table more than two feet high was leaning against the loess wall. A small broom made of bundled rice straw was placed on the table. Wang Lao'er took it and wiped the table, laughing, "Mr. Meng! Please sit down for a while, I'm really sorry!" Then he raised his head and said to the house, "Don't take care of these chickens, they've pooped all over the table." Meng Guobao saw that there were indeed a few wet marks on the table. He took out a small stool one foot high from the side of the table and sat down. He looked at the loess walls around and sighed, "Lao Er, I'm very ashamed!" Wang Lao'er tapped the head of his dry cigarette pipe on the edge of the table twice, knocking out the ashes. He tilted his head and pondered, seeming very surprised by his words. He looked at him and said, "Sir, what are you talking about?" Meng Guobao said: "Think about it! I dress better than you, eat better than you, and I don't have to work hard at all. You work hard all year round, but you live in such a house." Wang Lao'er laughed loudly and said, "Mr. Meng, you're really talking silly! You eat well, dress well, and don't have to work hard, that's what you cultivated in your previous life, what are you ashamed of?" Meng Guobao thought, this is really terrible! No matter what I say, he doesn't understand anything. However, this is not only Wang Lao'er, but also the people in my family are like this. It's really not an easy thing for someone to engage in the liberation of peasants and workers. The teacher in the classroom only tells us to start with liberating ourselves, what kind of liberation is mine? Alas! They don't understand anything, what can I say?

Film Special

Rare News from the Film Industry

Trivial Matters of "The Bird of Paradise" 236

— Bai

｜BirdofParadise

If you say this article is praising "The Bird of Paradise," I readily admit it: "The Bird of Paradise" indeed has many praiseworthy merits and facts.

㈠ Material Sacrifice

In January and February of this year, I read a piece of news in a report from the American film industry, roughly saying that Mr. King Vidor, director of RKO Pictures in America, and Ms. Dolores Del Rio, a female star, led three photographers to Hawaii to capture the background of "The Bird of Paradise." In Hawaii, they stayed at the Royal Hawaiian Hotel for more than two months. Upon returning to the United States, they presented their achievements: over one hundred landscape photos. Although it is said that the beauty of Hawaii's mountains and rivers is all contained within, the cost of this background test—including all travel expenses and film—was more than 500,000 yuan.

Constant spending, endless waste, meticulous research, verisimilitude; the Golden Country constantly wired money to Hawaii. After the film was completed, RKO Pictures' statistics showed that the entire film cost over 2.3 million US dollars, took nine months, and exceeded the budget in every aspect. The biggest reason was waiting for the eruption of the great Kilauea volcano to capture the real scenes of landslides, volcanic eruptions, ground fissures, and tsunamis. Four months were spent waiting and hoping in this state of inactivity.

According to the contract between RKO Pictures and Dolores, she had full authority to manage all expenses during filming in Hawaii. Upon settlement after completion, it was discovered that Dolores had spent more than double the budget. RKO Pictures, dissatisfied with this, canceled Dolores's contract for continued employment.

㈡ The Author's Tragic Encounters

Richard Walton Tully, the author of "The Bird of Paradise," experienced a tragic family breakdown because of this script. Therefore, before narrating Mr. Tully's misfortunes because of "The Bird of Paradise," let me tell some of his life's tragic history.

When Richard was thirteen years old, a flood ruined his father's assets, and he was financially hit. Richard became a theater vendor. He used his wages as a means to study. After graduating from high school, he decided to go to university. During his two years at the University of California, he worked diligently and took the time to write the script for the junior class performance. From many scripts, he actually won the top choice and was staged. Among the audience was Mrs. Fulsom Hans, who learned of the young Richard's hard work and struggle, so she provided financial assistance so that he could graduate from university. While Richard was consulting at the library, he became interested in the native Hawaiians: this was his motivation for writing the script for "The Bird of Paradise."

When "The Bird of Paradise" was staged, it was performed continuously for two years in New York and England. In an instant, Richard had become one of the wealthy men in New York. However, misfortune never left him, and he was suddenly accused of plagiarism. After six years of litigation, he was finally acquitted by the New York Court of Appeals on March 18, 1930.

He won the lawsuit, but he was penniless. At the same time, his wife divorced him. At this time, he only had a script, a full of bitterness, and empty sleeves!

RKO Pictures' purchase of the film adaptation rights to "The Bird of Paradise" was, of course, a turning point for him. This 55-year-old man—Richard—seeing "The Bird of Paradise" exhibited on the screen after the tragedy of death and family breakdown, perhaps a trace of bitter laughter would appear in his tearful face!

Film Review

A Review of "Svengali" 237

— Yan Nan

(Synopsis) An old and mysterious musician lives near three painters. The painters often tease the musician, but he is not offended. One day, the musician meets a young woman in the painters' house, whom he recognizes as a talented singer and greatly appreciates. However, the young woman and the youngest of the painters take a liking to each other at first sight, and love blossoms suddenly. The musician spares no effort to hypnotize the young woman and take her away. Years later, the musician and the woman's singing complement each other, and they are famous for a time. The painter tracks them down. One day, the musician, who is performing, dies on stage because he is exhausted and physically weak. However, the young woman's nature cannot be restored, so the painter's arrival ultimately fails to fulfill his long-cherished wish.

This script focuses on the word "demon," so the shots and lighting used are fully imbued with "mystery" and "greatness." In many places, ordinary things are stained with terrifying colors, truly standing out. The director must also have thought, and there is no cliché from beginning to end, only grasping the word "demon" to describe. The background is beautiful. The scenery also deeply shows "antique" and "mystery."

John Barrymore, who plays the musician, is the only protagonist. The makeup and costumes alone are already commendable. The performance is serious and stable, especially the illusory gaze, which is rare. Marian Marsh is a very harmonious assistant. The two different expressions, before and after being bewitched, reflect the musician's painstaking efforts, which is very good. Supporting roles such as Bramwell Fletcher, who plays the young painter, are also very competent. Although the remaining people have few performances, their results are good. Everyone has a "classical" style.

This is one of Warner's best productions ever shown at the Carlton.

A Glimpse of Opinions

㈠ The Issue of Lowering Ticket Prices 238

— Yu Lun

The downstairs seat prices in the first-class theaters in this city, except for Cathay and Grand, only cost 60 cents, which is already much more accessible to ordinary people than the minimum of one dollar a few years ago. This is thanks to the Nanjing Grand Theater. Before it opened, theaters such as the Odeon, Carlton, and Summer Palace were all showing first-run films, and the lowest seat price during the day was still one dollar. Since Nanjing set the example of charging 60 cents, theaters have followed suit and reduced prices. Later, the opening of Da Guangming and Xin Guang also charged 60 cents. It seems very cheap to see a first-run film for 60 cents, and there is no possibility of further reduction. In fact, that is not true, it can be reduced a little more. Hong Kong is a good example.

The entertainment venues in Hong Kong, such as Queen's and Central, are all magnificent theaters that show first-run films. The Entertainment Theatre even has hot and cold air pipes. Their seat prices are 50 cents for Entertainment and the same for Central, and only 35 cents for Queen's.

According to the above reasons, the ticket prices of Nanjing and others can be lower, because if the ticket prices are reduced, the film rental can also be reduced, and the theaters will not suffer a big loss. But there may be difficulties, because if the ticket prices are reduced, people in the middle class will also go to first-class theaters to see movies, and the business of second-class theaters will be hit. Moreover, the order in the first-class theaters will not be too orderly, right?

㈡ Avoid Defamatory Criticism 239

"It's a Chinese film, not worth watching!" This argument is a common estimate among film-loving audiences when choosing a film. It is an unfounded, defamatory criticism, which invisibly inflicts deep wounds on domestic films! Needless to say, this is the main aspect of the many reasons why domestic films are not promoted.

Art, like social phenomena, is evolving day by day. Look! Domestic films, still in their youth, are booming. We should use our full strength to love, protect, and cultivate them. We should often watch domestic films and give them honest criticism: directors and actors must especially accept the criticism of the audience as much as possible. If they promote each other in this way, domestic films will be able to make great strides in artistic development!

The audience should first understand domestic films before making criticism: if it is just an unfounded estimate, it is easy to injure domestic films! People who love movies should avoid defamatory criticism.

Casual Talk

The Movement of Makeup 240

— Hong

We know that modern movies can use their unique lenses to capture all kinds of unique characters, but we must know that these all kinds of unique characters cannot be successful without miraculous makeup.

Makeup in Hollywood, the Golden Country, has already been successful, but our Chinese film actors know very little about this, and of course, there is no talk of research. Therefore, we are now specifically raising this issue to awaken the attention of Chinese film actors!

Chinese movie stars, do not think that you already understand that old men should use × oil paint and × powder, and young people and beautiful women should use..., these superficialities are enough to satisfy you. You should also understand how to cover up the blemishes on your face, even out the color of your face, so that it is conducive to photography.

However, our Chinese movie stars have not firmly grasped this weapon of makeup. Let us cite an example, such as the most popular female star today, Ms. Hu Die, no matter what kind of role she plays, we can always recognize her as Hu Die from the same two dimples!

Let's look at a deceased male star in Hollywood, the success of Lon Chaney, and the infinite glory he left in film history, is entirely due to his knowledge of how to use this miraculous weapon of makeup.

Therefore, I advise Chinese film actors to carefully examine the characteristics that the character in the play should have before going on camera and when putting on makeup. At the same time, they should also pay attention to the harmony of the tones between the several people on the stage throughout the play. Then start, cover up and decorate, so that it is neither too much nor too little, and spiritualize it. Then you can get half the certainty of your success on the screen.

Finally, I hope that our Chinese movie stars will cleverly use this weapon—makeup.

Film Industry Investigation

About Lianhua's Third Studio 241

— Hong

｜A Visit to a Film Production Company, Part Nine

The establishment of Lianhua Film Production Company has the ambition to seize the leadership of the Chinese film industry, and it can also be said to be the trustification of the Chinese film industry. Its sphere of influence has expanded from Shanghai, the Hollywood of China, to Beiping and Hong Kong. Therefore, Lianhua established a third production studio in Hong Kong last spring and opened a film talent training institute: Mr. Li Beihai, a senior in the film industry, presided over the matter, and then searched for film professionals from Guangdong and Hong Kong, such as Liang Shaopo and Guan Wenqing, to help with the work. After a considerable period of preparation, it began its film production work.

The maiden work of Lianhua's Third Studio was "Iron Bone Orchid Heart," written by the famous playwright Liang Shaopo, co-starring Shi Youyu and Feng Jiezhen, and directed by Guan Wenqing. This play has been shown in Shanghai for a long time, and it has a strong local color and is full of Cantonese flavor.

The second production was "Cuckoo's Cry in the Ancient Temple," a script written by Luo Mingyou himself, directed by Liang Shaopo, and starring Xue Zhaorong and Tang Xingtut. It was filmed at the end of last year. It is also a play about Cantonese people.

As for the third production, although the script "Wise Mother" written by Li Beihai has been selected, it has not been realized. It has not been put into the camera work. In this world economic panic and commercial depression, Lianhua's Third Studio has stopped invisibly.

However, whether it can continue to produce films in the future, it is not dare to say for sure now.

Film Studio Gossip

Lin Chuchu and Xuan Jinglin 242

— Tang Shen

There are two female stars in the Chinese film industry. Neither of them has beautiful faces, but they both have sad personalities: one is Li Minwei's wife, Lin Chuchu, and the other is Xuan Jinglin, known as the Little Old Woman.

Marean Nixon Robbed 243

— Zhen Hua

Two months ago, Marean Nixon and her husband, Edward Hillman, were happily living in their Beverly Hills home. Unexpectedly, they suddenly received a threatening letter asking them to borrow a large sum of money, but they turned a deaf ear to it. Soon after, they announced that they would travel to Europe. Unfortunately, they were robbed in a car while traveling in Europe. Afterwards, they lost a total of four hundred yuan in cash and many valuable jewelry. In addition, Marean suffered a pointless scare. Fortunately, the bandits were captured a few days later, but they were very afraid of the bandits' revenge in the future. Therefore, they hired several strong and capable bodyguards who followed her all day long.

Film Monographs

"Dare You!?" 244

— Chen Dabei

The previous nine expression solo practice methods used a deep breathing progressive retreat method of practice because they wanted scholars to develop a habit of being able to self-consciously move their own expressions.

Now we want to go a step further and use the power of sound to help our expressions. Originally, expressions are divided into two types. The first type is gestural expression, which moves people through sight. The second type is sound expression, which moves people through hearing. What we have practiced is only the most important part of gestural expression. Currently, because of space limitations, we have to show part of the power of sound expression.

This is the tenth style of expression solo practice. It is roughly similar to the second style discussed in detail above. However, this is to use sound to increase the power of expression without deep breathing.

Scholars still follow the previous method to focus on the center of their eyebrows in the mirror, and then deeply inhale a breath from their nostrils. When inhaling, the eyes gradually become angry.

You first carefully observe the extent of your angry expression. Then shout "Dare you!?" at the shadow in the mirror. At the same time, your fists and arms also do their best to help. Then see how much the expression has increased.
